              serviceWorkerParam: { scope: "/wp-content/plugins/onesignal-free-web-push-notifications/sdk_files/push/onesignal/" },
              serviceWorkerPath: "OneSignalSDKWorker.js",
            });
          });

          // Unregister the legacy OneSignal service worker to prevent scope conflicts
          if (navigator.serviceWorker) {
            navigator.serviceWorker.getRegistrations().then((registrations) => {
              // Iterate through all registered service workers
              registrations.forEach((registration) => {
                // Check the script URL to identify the specific service worker
                if (registration.active && registration.active.scriptURL.includes('OneSignalSDKWorker.js.php')) {
                  // Unregister the service worker
                  registration.unregister().then((success) => {
                    if (success) {
                      console.log('OneSignalSW: Successfully unregistered:', registration.active.scriptURL);
                    } else {
                      console.log('OneSignalSW: Failed to unregister:', registration.active.scriptURL);
                    }
                  });
                }
              });
            }).catch((error) => {
              console.error('Error fetching service worker registrations:', error);
            });
        }
        </script>

            <p class="fw-copytext">Solar panels are the true money-making machines of your solar power setup. These powerhouses capture sunlight and convert it into DC electricity, starting the process of generating renewable energy for your home. High-quality solar panels are essential for maximizing energy production and ensuring that you get the most out of your investment. With efficient solar panels, you can significantly reduce your energy bills and contribute to a more sustainable future.</p>

            <span class="msf-h2">The Inverter – The Heart of Your Solar Power System</span>
            <p class="fw-copytext">The inverter is the brain of your solar power setup. It efficiently converts the DC electricity generated by your solar panels into the AC electricity needed to power your home. This crucial step ensures that the energy harnessed from the sun is transformed into a usable form for all your household appliances. Without a high-quality inverter, your solar energy system cannot operate effectively, making this component essential for maximizing your renewable energy benefits.</p>

			<span class="sbi-screenreader">Net Billing changed the equation.

Under old net m</span>
									<img decoding="async" src="https://zorays.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed/img/placeholder.png" alt="Net Billing changed the equation.

Under old net metering, exported units offset imported units. Simple.

Under net billing, you buy high and sell low.
That spread destroys passive ROI.

So the strategy shifts.

Net Billing → Hybrid Solution → ROI Math.

Instead of exporting at undervalued rates, you:

• Consume your own solar first
• Store excess in Lithium BESS
• Use stored power during peak tariff hours
• Reduce expensive grid imports

Example:

Consume 500 units
Produce 400 units

Under net billing:
You buy 500 at ~Rs33
You sell 400 at ~Rs10

Spread hurts.

But with Hybrid + Battery:

Day solar runs loads.
Excess stored.
Night loads run on stored energy.
Grid draw minimized.

That is how ROI is protected.

Policy changed.
Engineering must respond.

#NetBilling #HybridSolar #LithiumBESS #SolarPakistan #EnergyStorage #SolarROI #ZoraysSolar" aria-hidden="true" loading="lazy">
		</a>

<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element  vc_custom_1740647571243" style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<p>Solar panels in Pakistan (as per <strong data-start="33" data-end="49">Zorays Solar</strong> pricing) now cost around <strong data-start="75" data-end="100">PKR 32 to 35 per watt</strong> for Tier 1 panels. A <strong data-start="122" data-end="136">585W panel</strong> would range from <strong data-start="154" data-end="178">PKR 18,720 to 20,475</strong> as of <strong data-start="185" data-end="202">Jan 1, 2026</strong>. For a complete system quote tailored to your site, <strong data-start="255" data-end="271">Zorays Solar</strong> offers expert guidance and the latest pricing.</p>

<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element " style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<h4>How many solar panels do I need?</h4>
	</div>
</div>




<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element  vc_custom_1740647639073" style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<p data-start="0" data-end="221">The number of solar panels you need depends on your monthly electricity usage and available roof space. With <strong data-start="109" data-end="124">585W panels</strong>, a <strong data-start="128" data-end="143">10kW system</strong> (covering around <strong data-start="161" data-end="186">3,000 units per month</strong>) would need about <strong data-start="205" data-end="218">17 panels</strong>.</p>
<p data-start="223" data-end="334" data-is-last-node="" data-is-only-node="">For a quick and accurate estimate tailored to your needs, you can also check <strong data-start="300" data-end="333"><a href="https://zorays.com/calculator" target="_new" rel="noopener" data-start="302" data-end="331">https://zorays.com/calculator</a></strong>.</p>
	</div>
</div>




		</div> 
	</div>
	</div> 
</div></div></div></div></div><div class="cell "><div class="inner-wrap-outer"><div class="inner-wrap" ><div id="fws_699d90e713063" data-midnight="" data-column-margin="default" class="wpb_row vc_row-fluid vc_row inner_row"  style=""><div class="row-bg-wrap"> <div class="row-bg" ></div> </div><div class="row_col_wrap_12_inner col span_12  left">
	<div  class="vc_col-sm-12 wpb_column column_container vc_column_container col child_column centered-text padding-2-percent el_spacing_10px inherit_tablet no-extra-padding_phone "   data-padding-pos="all" data-has-bg-color="false" data-bg-color="" data-bg-opacity="1" data-animation="" data-delay="0" >
		<div class="vc_column-inner" >
		<div class="wpb_wrapper">
			
<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element " style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<h4>How solar panels work?</h4>
	</div>
</div>




<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element  vc_custom_1740647704171" style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<p data-start="0" data-end="328">Solar panels work by converting <strong data-start="32" data-end="61">sunlight into electricity</strong> using <strong data-start="68" data-end="95">photovoltaic (PV) cells</strong>. When sunlight hits these cells, it knocks electrons loose, creating <strong data-start="165" data-end="190">a flow of electricity</strong>. This <strong data-start="197" data-end="215">DC electricity</strong> is then converted into <strong data-start="239" data-end="257">AC electricity</strong> through an <strong data-start="269" data-end="281">inverter</strong>, making it usable for your home or business.</p>
<p data-start="330" data-end="391">In short: <strong data-start="340" data-end="389">Sunlight → Electricity → Power for your home.</strong></p>
	</div>
</div>




		</div> 
	</div>
	</div> 
</div></div></div></div></div><div class="cell "><div class="inner-wrap-outer"><div class="inner-wrap" ><div id="fws_699d90e71379d" data-midnight="" data-column-margin="default" class="wpb_row vc_row-fluid vc_row inner_row"  style=""><div class="row-bg-wrap"> <div class="row-bg" ></div> </div><div class="row_col_wrap_12_inner col span_12  left">
	<div  class="vc_col-sm-12 wpb_column column_container vc_column_container col child_column centered-text padding-2-percent el_spacing_10px inherit_tablet no-extra-padding_phone "   data-padding-pos="all" data-has-bg-color="false" data-bg-color="" data-bg-opacity="1" data-animation="" data-delay="0" >
		<div class="vc_column-inner" >
		<div class="wpb_wrapper">
			
<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element " style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<h4>Are solar panels worth it?</h4>
	</div>
</div>




<div class="wpb_text_column wpb_content_element  vc_custom_1740647804405" style=" max-width: 375px; display: inline-block;">
	<div class="wpb_wrapper">
		<p>Absolutely, <strong data-start="12" data-end="41">solar panels are worth it</strong>, especially in Pakistan where <strong data-start="72" data-end="96">sunlight is abundant</strong> and <strong data-start="101" data-end="134">electricity prices are rising</strong>. With net metering, you can <strong data-start="163" data-end="192">export excess electricity</strong> to the grid and <strong data-start="209" data-end="229">reduce your bill</strong>. Plus, systems typically <strong data-start="255" data-end="295">pay back their cost within 3-5 years</strong>, after which you enjoy <strong data-start="319" data-end="357">free electricity for over 20 years</strong>.</p>
	</div>
</div>




		</div> 
	</div>
	</div>

</div><div class="toggles accordion toggles--minimal-shadow" data-br="20px" data-starting="default" data-style="minimal"><div class="toggle default" data-inner-wrap="true"><h3 class="toggle-title"><a href="#" role="button" class="nectar-inherit-h3 toggle-heading"><i role="presentation" class="fa fa-plus-circle"></i>How much does a solar panel cost in Pakistan?</a></h3><div><div class="inner-toggle-wrap"><div class="nectar-responsive-text font_size_min_14px font_size_max_20px font_size_desktop_1-1vw font_line_height_1-6 nectar-link-underline-effect"><p>How much are solar panels? As of the price update in Jan 2026, the cost of a solar panel in Pakistan depends on factors like capacity, brand, and quality. On average, a standard 580-watt panel can range from PKR 15,950 to PKR 18,125. However, prices may have changed since then due to market dynamics and technological advancements.</p>
</div></div></div></div><div class="toggle default" data-inner-wrap="true"><h3 class="toggle-title"><a href="#" role="button" class="nectar-inherit-h3 toggle-heading"><i role="presentation" class="fa fa-plus-circle"></i>Which is the best solar system in Pakistan?</a></h3><div><div class="inner-toggle-wrap"><div class="nectar-responsive-text font_size_min_14px font_size_max_20px font_size_desktop_1-1vw font_line_height_1-6 nectar-link-underline-effect"><p>The selection of what you can call the best solar system in Pakistan depends on individual needs, budget, and specific requirements. Worldwide renowned brands like Jinko,  Longi,  Trina,  JA,  FirstSolar,  Sunpower,  REC,  and Canadian Solar are known for producing high-quality solar panels; whereas, Tesla,  Refusol,  SMA,  ABB,  Schneider,  Outback, and Huawei are solar inverter manufacturers and the best solar companies in Pakistan choose from amongst them.</p>
</div></div></div></div><div class="toggle default" data-inner-wrap="true"><h3 class="toggle-title"><a href="#" role="button" class="nectar-inherit-h3 toggle-heading"><i role="presentation" class="fa fa-plus-circle"></i>How many solar panels are required for a 1.5 ton AC in Pakistan?</a></h3><div><div class="inner-toggle-wrap"><div class="nectar-responsive-text font_size_min_14px font_size_max_20px font_size_desktop_1-1vw font_line_height_1-6 nectar-link-underline-effect"><p>A 1.5 ton AC typically consumes around 1.5 kW of power per hour. To run it for an hour using solar energy, you would need a solar panel system capable of generating at least 1.5 kW of power. This would generally require at least four 550-watt solar panels, assuming they receive optimal sunlight. Keep in mind that factors like panel efficiency and local climate conditions can influence the exact number of panels needed. Consulting with our solar experts for a personalized <a href="https://zorays.com/solar-air-conditioner/">solar on ac</a> assessment is recommended.</p>

    <h1 style="color:#5000e6;">Zorays Realtime Analytics</h1>
    <p style="font-weight:500;">GA4 Property: <strong>289319621</strong></p>

        <div id="active_users_chart" style="width:100%;height:250px;"></div>
        <h2 id="active_count" style="font-size:48px;color:#00A859;font-weight:700;">0</h2>
        <p style="color:#666;">Active visitors exploring the solar future 🌞</p>

<script src="https://www.gstatic.com/charts/loader.js"></script>
<script>
google.charts.load('current', {'packages':['gauge']});
google.charts.setOnLoadCallback(fetchRealtime);

function fetchRealtime(){
    fetch(ajaxurl+'?action=zorays_get_ga_data')
        .then(r=>r.json())
        .then(res=>{
            if(!res.success) throw res.data;
            document.getElementById('zorays_loader').style.display='none';
            document.getElementById('zorays_dashboard').style.display='block';
            drawRealtime(res.data.activeUsers || 0);
        })
        .catch(e=>document.getElementById('zorays_loader').innerHTML=e);
}

function drawRealtime(u){
    // Fancy gauge
    const g=google.visualization.arrayToDataTable([['Label','Users'],['Active',u]]);
    const chart=new google.visualization.Gauge(document.getElementById('active_users_chart'));
    chart.draw(g,{width:400,height:200,greenFrom:1,greenTo:20,yellowFrom:20,yellowTo:50,redFrom:50,redTo:100,minorTicks:5});

    // Smooth animation number
    const el=document.getElementById('active_count');
    let prev=parseInt(el.textContent)||0;
    const step=(u-prev)/20;
    let frame=0;
    const animate=()=>{ 
        frame++;
        el.textContent=Math.round(prev+step*frame);
        if(frame<20) requestAnimationFrame(animate);
    };
    animate();
}

setInterval(fetchRealtime,20000);
</script>
